  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_61b73f1f-68fc-474b-9030-e33a3313afdc'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3396766353292450220">With each and every new novel, Dean Koontz raises the stakes--and the pulse rate--higher than any other author. Now, in what may be his most suspenseful and heartfelt novel ever, he brings us the story of an ordinary man whose extraordinary commitment to his wife will take him on a harrowing journey of adventure, sacrifice, and redemption to the mystery of love itself--and</span>
  <span id="freeText3396766353292450220" style="display:none">With each and every new novel, Dean Koontz raises the stakes--and the pulse rate--higher than any other author. Now, in what may be his most suspenseful and heartfelt novel ever, he brings us the story of an ordinary man whose extraordinary commitment to his wife will take him on a harrowing journey of adventure, sacrifice, and redemption to the mystery of love itself--and to a showdown with the darkness that would destroy it forever. <br />What would you do for love? Would you die? Would you kill? <br />We have your wife. You can get her back for two million cash. Landscaper Mitchell Rafferty thinks it must be some kind of joke. He was in the middle of planting impatiens in the yard of one of his clients when his cell phone rang. Now he's standing in a normal suburban neighborhood on a bright summer day, having a phone conversation out of his darkest nightmare. <br />Whoever is on the other end of the line is dead serious. He has Mitch's wife and he's named the price for her safe return. The caller doesn't care that Mitch runs a small two-man landscaping operation and has no way of raising such a vast sum. He's confident that Mitch will find a way. <br />If he loves his wife enough. . . Mitch does love her enough. He loves her more than life itself. He's got seventy-two hours to prove it. He has to find the two million by then. But he'll pay a lot more. He'll pay anything. <br />From its tense opening to its shattering climax, The Husband is a thriller that will hold you in its relentless grip for every twist, every shock, every revelation...until it lets you go, unmistakably changed. This is a Dean Koontz novel, after all. And there's no other experience quite like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3396766353292450220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743779812" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743779812?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553589092" href="/book/show/157525.The_Husband">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743779812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2965752249564782672"><b>
  <u>I liked it but it wasn't as good as my old Koontz's books</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>BACK TO KOONTZ</u>
</b><br/><br/>There was a while since I had read a new novel by Dean Koontz, well, at least a new novel to me, and I was quite excited to read this one.<br/><br/>I thought that the premise was very good...<br/><br/>A husband is threatened by some unknown people kidnapping his wife and demanding two million dollars, that indeed he doesn't have and he hadn't the least clue of how to get it.<br/><br/>The book is divided in three parts, and I think that the first p</span>
  <span id="freeText2965752249564782672" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>I liked it but it wasn't as good as my old Koontz's books</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BACK TO KOONTZ</u>
</b><br /><br />There was a while since I had read a new novel by Dean Koontz, well, at least a new novel to me, and I was quite excited to read this one.<br /><br />I thought that the premise was very good...<br /><br />A husband is threatened by some unknown people kidnapping his wife and demanding two million dollars, that indeed he doesn't have and he hadn't the least clue of how to get it.<br /><br />The book is divided in three parts, and I think that the first part is the more solid one of the whole book, since you are in the same boat that the main character, the husband, you know only what he knows and that's a brilliant way to manage a thriller. <br /><br />However, just at the end of the first part you started to know events of other places and from other characters so, many of the mystery is getting to lose its strength and with that a pretty good part of the excitement is getting weaker.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>KEEP THINGS SIMPLE</u>
</b><br /><br />I think that the basic premise was just enough to build a quite good thriller, the husband fighting alone against the world to save his wife.<br /><br />However, the story gets more complicated reaching some too far-fetched levels, that in my opinion were totally unnecessary.<br /><br />It saturated a story that it could way simpler.<br /><br />I have to admit that some of the twists in the story have a lot of air of a Hitchcock film, that in my opinion it's a big compliment coming from me.<br /><br />However, I supposed that all it's about expectations and some of those twists were against my initial expectations for the novel, so instead to increase my reading experience with the book, it got more erratic and/or harder to accept it.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>KEEP THE PACE</u>
</b><br /><br />While the book started with engines kicking to full speed, avoiding a singlee rest to the reader...<br /><br />...when the second part of the book started, there were too many chapters, in my humble opinion.<br /><br />In a plot that it could be solved a lot quicker and simpler, giving a better overall reading experience to the read, one ends with a book spreading more than necessary.<br /><br />Finally, in the climax part (I won't spoil it, don't worry!), many of the main threat got weaker, and not by actions of the main character, so it's a bummer, and some interesting twists that were arising are left without exploiting their whole potential.<br /><br />The story is solved too easy to my taste.<br /><br />But I can't deny that I liked enough the reading of the novel, but definitely it could be quite better.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2965752249564782672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_12652443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12652443" />
    <a title="Todd Greene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53248-todd-greene"><img alt="Todd Greene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523968948p2/53248.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12652443?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Todd Greene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Todd Greene" href="/user/show/53248-todd-greene">Todd Greene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553589092" href="/book/show/157525.The_Husband">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">adults, teens</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12652443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8960658279685629605">I've always thought of Dean Koontz as the master of psychological suspense. His novels are aways full of weird and over the top characters that he makes believable and then he puts them in situations which are weird and over the top and makes them believable.<br/><br/>This time around Dean changes things up a bit. He takes an average Joe and puts him in a seemingly no win situation. Mitch Rafferty, owner of a two man landscaping business gets the phone call no husband would want. Someone has his wife. Tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8960658279685629605" style="display:none">I've always thought of Dean Koontz as the master of psychological suspense. His novels are aways full of weird and over the top characters that he makes believable and then he puts them in situations which are weird and over the top and makes them believable.<br /><br />This time around Dean changes things up a bit. He takes an average Joe and puts him in a seemingly no win situation. Mitch Rafferty, owner of a two man landscaping business gets the phone call no husband would want. Someone has his wife. That's the bad news. The worse news is, the someone wants $2 million in 60 hours. He doesn't have that kind of money and they know it. Still, they're convinced he'll find away to get the funds. If he loves his wife. He loves her. No question.<br /><br />The kidnappers tighten the screws from that moment on by first killing someone "innocent" so Mitch will know they mean business. Things go down hill for our hero from there.<br /><br />One of the things I really liked about this story was how Dean shows two people who were raised in the same dysfunctional environment could respond to that upbringing in totally different ways. You'll have to read the book to find out what I mean. I try to never include plot spoilers in my reviews.<br /><br />I gave a rating of 5 stars because I loved the story. Koontz in one of my all time favorite novelists. I dream of one day writing my own novels half as well as he does. However, this novel wasn't without its problems for me.<br /><br />One, the scenes with the wife when she's held captive just didn't work for me. When I read the sections with Mitch it was like I was right there with him. Almost like what happened to him happened to me. With those sections devoted to his wife I felt somehow distant from the situation. I don't know why. I don't believe this is the desired affect Dean meant.<br /><br />The second thing I didn't care for was just a pet peeve of mine and it didn't really take away from the story. Most stories have this same element in them. I've just never understood why. Here's what I'm talking about. The novel is 68 chapters. In chapter one Mitch learns of his wife's kidnapping. From chapter two on Mitch is doing everything he can to get her back. After all that can happen happens, we come to chapter 68. It's 3 years later and everything is normal again.<br /><br />What's the rub for me? Mitch did some pretty terrible and even illegal things in an attempt to get his wife back. Seemingly, there were no repercussions for his actions. I know one would say he was justified, but I'm just not sure how the law would take this in the real world.<br /><br />Maybe that's the point. It's not real life, it's a novel. And a great thrill ride it is.<br /><br />Pick up a copy and see what you think. I believe you won't be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8960658279685629605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78616383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78616383" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78616383?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007226566" href="/book/show/906896.The_Husband">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2009">read-in-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78616383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer416287390589583890">This books contains the funniest simile ever: The man character drives his car and is accompanied by <i> The hobgoblins of wind</i>. Yes, HOBGOBLINS OF WIND.<br/><br/>Okay, so I've read <i>The Husband</i> when it came out and forgot it entirely. Deciding to write a review of it, I grabbed a paperback and began to read.<br/><br/><i>The Husband</i> is one of those airport books that will keep your attention during the flight, but you can leave them on the plane without feeling any guilt. Character development is practically nonexistant. </span>
  <span id="freeText416287390589583890" style="display:none">This books contains the funniest simile ever: The man character drives his car and is accompanied by <i> The hobgoblins of wind</i>. Yes, HOBGOBLINS OF WIND.<br /><br />Okay, so I've read <i>The Husband</i> when it came out and forgot it entirely. Deciding to write a review of it, I grabbed a paperback and began to read.<br /><br /><i>The Husband</i> is one of those airport books that will keep your attention during the flight, but you can leave them on the plane without feeling any guilt. Character development is practically nonexistant. But it's all about the plot, eh? The book starts with a bang: A gardener's wife is kidnapped, and the kidnappers want 2 million dollars. Obviously, a gardener doesn't have such money, but the kidnappers are serious - they shoot an innocent passerby just to prove it.<br /><br />It all gets better and better from here. As I was reading I kept saying "hey Dean ,it'sa not bad, not bad at all!". Sure, the characters are bland, the villains are bland, but who cares, it's not a book that you'd read for school. The tension keeps increasing, and our gardener finds himself in situations that neither he nor the reader could have expected.<br /><br />Until the end.<br /><br />Koontz has been carefully building his house of cards to impress the reader, but at the very end he gets like "whew, who gives a crap anyway!" and blows the whole thing down. It crashes painfully and ruins the whole experience. <br />Because there's absolutely no need to even try to explain how the gardener got out of the mess he has made. He committed various things, illegal of course, and there are no repercussions. All we get is "3 YEARS LATER" 1 page epilogue where everyone is happy and sappy. Not one word is devoted to any sort of explanation. Which one might think would come, if there were whole pages devoted to Koontz's philosophy and the whole book was written in his "new" prose, short sentences being interrupted by paragraphs of some new-age bullshit. Yes, describing the inspirational grass is absolutely necessary, but satisfying the reader is not. You're wondering how Koontz will tie up all the loose ends? Here's your answer: he doesn't do it at all.<br /><br />This could have been an enjoyable beach read, but Koontz decided to write another 50 books that year so he had to call it quits. Shame on you, Dean.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="416287390589583890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17665803492876210226">I read this book in about a day, and I really enjoyed it. One of the things I love about reading a Dean Koontz book is that I can pretty much tell just by the fact that he wrote it that it will be a good read.<br/><br/>This book follows a man who is trying to ransom his kidnapped wife. It explores the elastic nature of human morality and is full of twists and turns. Mitch (the protagonist) is a simple gardener who finds his life turned upside down in the blink of an eye. He is forced to alter his entire p</span>
  <span id="freeText17665803492876210226" style="display:none">I read this book in about a day, and I really enjoyed it. One of the things I love about reading a Dean Koontz book is that I can pretty much tell just by the fact that he wrote it that it will be a good read.<br /><br />This book follows a man who is trying to ransom his kidnapped wife. It explores the elastic nature of human morality and is full of twists and turns. Mitch (the protagonist) is a simple gardener who finds his life turned upside down in the blink of an eye. He is forced to alter his entire perspective on good and bad, right and wrong in order to save the life of his wife.<br /><br />This book doesn't have some of the mystical/sci-fi properties of other Koontz books, but it keeps the action up just the same. <br /><br />There are several other authors that I have read over time who have become predictable in their plot devices and story lines, and I am pleased to say that after 20 years of reading Dean Koontz novels, he still surprises me.<br /><br />Also, I love that in the back of his book he gives his address for fans to write to, and if you listen to his podcast you know that he and his wife answer every letter that is sent. That is one good man.</span>

  <span id="freeText3275956990676816245" style="display:none">I envy the simple life that Mitch and Holly have created for themselves. I agree with Holly's belief that we create our own realities (this idea was also presented in By The Light of the Moon, one of my favorites by Dean Koontz). I also believe in Mitch's belief that there is meaning to be found. <br /><br />Having recently read Intensity of June 2017, and The Husband in July 2017 - I found a connection in the phrase "untouched and alive", Chyna's mantra. In The Husband, the phrase is reversed to "alive and untouched."<br /><br />The Husband is better than The Darkest Evening of the Year, Your Heart Belongs to Me and Breathless, but not in the top-tier category of From The Corner of His Eye, By The Light of the Moon, Cold Fire, False Memory, The Voice of The Night ... just to name a few :-) <br /><br />Favorite Passages:<br /><br /><i>"Maybe that's what a hero is - someone who instinctively does the right thing."<br />______<br /><br />.... he seemed to be gaining for what he had lost, what so quickly healed the hole in him, was a capacity for awe, a deeper sense of the mystery of all things. <br />Then he pulled back from the brink of awe, to terror and to grim determination. <br />______<br /><br />He had to do what he didn't want to do, because whether the sonofabitch was a carcass or unconscious, he possessed a weapon. Mitch needed a weapon. And quick.<br />______<br /><br />A pair of synchronized spiders, his hands crept left to right across the surface, testing. He pressed gently, and then a little harder.<br />______<br /><br />"YOU'RE A BAD SONOFABITCH, A BAD, BAD SONOFABITCH!"</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3275956990676816245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_329329951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329329951" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329329951?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329329951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14018256636872185496">THE HUSBAND Review This could possibly be the last good Dean Koontz novel. I only say "possibly" because I have yet to read RELENTLESS, which was published after this one, and do not hold high hopes for me liking it.<br/> <br/>Written in 2006, three years after the stellar debut of Pico Mundo's paranormally-inclined fry cook, THE HUSBAND avoids all the typical Koontz trappings. There's no witty/sarcastic narrator, no uber smart Golden, no blond female lead, no unrealistic dialogue, absolutely zero filler,</span>
  <span id="freeText14018256636872185496" style="display:none">THE HUSBAND Review This could possibly be the last good Dean Koontz novel. I only say "possibly" because I have yet to read RELENTLESS, which was published after this one, and do not hold high hopes for me liking it.<br /> <br />Written in 2006, three years after the stellar debut of Pico Mundo's paranormally-inclined fry cook, THE HUSBAND avoids all the typical Koontz trappings. There's no witty/sarcastic narrator, no uber smart Golden, no blond female lead, no unrealistic dialogue, absolutely zero filler, and not a hint of quirky, preposterous, mustache-twirling villainous types. <br /> <br />There's something truly fresh about this book, and I think what stands out the most is, Koontz actually managed to scare me again. There are more than a few scenes from the kidnapped wife's POV that chilled me to the bone. One especially terrifying chapter has the kidnapper's voice circling her in the darkness, drawing closer, drifting away, leaning in, ebbing... sometimes it's so close that she fears he's about to kiss her. I'm not doing justice to the scene, but suffice to say that, after reading it, I needed a space heater to thaw the blood in my veins. I haven't felt that way during a Koontz novel since reading DRAGON TEARS in 1993, and I think that novel only scared me because I was 13 years old. Back then, Barney the Big Purple Pedophile scared the shit out of me.<br /> <br />Our main character, Mitch, is a likable enough guy, but by the end of THE HUSBAND, he's a broken individual. He manages some pretty nasty and twisted things after finding out why his wife was kidnapped. If I'd been in Mitch's shoes, well... the song "Five Minutes Alone", by Pantera, comes to mind. Needless to say, I still rooted for the man Mitch became, but I was a tad more fearful of him than for him.<br /> <br />In the last Koontz book I read, the MC (a pastry chef) droned on and on about this baked good or that tasty confection. It was useless information, and as boring as turtle sex. Koontz is also known for describing at length plantlife in exceedingly banal prose. When I first started THE HUSBAND and found out that the MC was a gardener, I almost slammed the book closed. I thought, "Wonderful... now he has a reason to bore me to death," but I continued to read. Boy, am I ever glad I did.<br /> <br />The ending ties everything up nicely if a bit too quickly. But I think the finale only speeds by because the middle of the book is so well paced. Koontz had me on the edge of my seat for over 95% of this book, so much so that I didn't want the ride to end. Sweet baby Tom Cruise, I wish he still wrote like this. I did deduct half a star for the tacked-on final chapter. It read as if someone told Koontz: "You have to say something about what happened afterward. Toss in a one-page epilogue of sorts and call it a day." To which Koontz responded: "Fuckin' A. I'm on that shit like scars on John Wayne Bobbit!" The final thousand words of THE HUSBAND are so rushed and heartless you'll feel as if you've just been raped by a rabbit that suffers from premature ejaculation, leaving you with this final thought: "That was brief and uncalled for."<br /> <br />In summation, should you choose to read a Dean Koontz book from this century, pick up THE HUSBAND. It won't win any literary awards, but it's a tense thriller by a former master of suspense. This is Koontz on his game, and it shouldn't be missed. Highly recommended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14018256636872185496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1781408607732232950">Audiobook performed by Holter Graham<br/>3.5*** <br/><br/>Mitch Rafferty runs a small, 2-man, landscaping business. He’s in the middle of planting impatiens in a client’s yard when he gets a call on his cell-phone. His wife starts with “Whatever happens, I love you.” Then the kidnapper gets on the line and demands $2 million. There must be some mistake; he and his wife have less than $12,000 to their name. But the kidnapper is adamant that “If you love your wife enough” Mitch will find a way to come up with th</span>
  <span id="freeText1781408607732232950" style="display:none">Audiobook performed by Holter Graham<br />3.5*** <br /><br />Mitch Rafferty runs a small, 2-man, landscaping business. He’s in the middle of planting impatiens in a client’s yard when he gets a call on his cell-phone. His wife starts with “Whatever happens, I love you.” Then the kidnapper gets on the line and demands $2 million. There must be some mistake; he and his wife have less than $12,000 to their name. But the kidnapper is adamant that “If you love your wife enough” Mitch will find a way to come up with the ransom in time. <br /><br />Well, this was a wild ride! The formula is pretty standard, and I was pretty certain the “good guys” would win. Trouble is, who are the “good guys”? Koontz includes multiple twists in the plot so that every time I thought I had figured it out, I was proven wrong. The ending felt rushed and unfinished to me, but I definitely enjoyed the ride. <br /><br />This is the first book by Koontz that I’ve read. It’s not great literature, but it sure held my attention and I’ll definitely read more from him. Especially when I’m in the mood for a fast-paced, entertaining thriller.<br /><br />Holter Graham does a fine job narrating the audio version. He has good pacing and I believed in the characters as he voiced them. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1781408607732232950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_903432751" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/903432751" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/903432751?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-concept-poor-execution">great-concept-poor-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer903432751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8232573838728338777">One would expect with a storyline revolving around an average Joe struggling to ransom his kidnapped wife back that it'd be super intense and keep me on the edge of my seat, right?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398005087ra/9356418.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It dragged on and on and the writing wasn't something I'd expect from a bestselling author. It was sketchy and the dialogue at times was just plain awkward.<br/><br/>There were some moments that made me sit up, but those were far and in-between and mostly had to do with the wife, Holly. The husband, Mitch was a fucking pansy and</span>
  <span id="freeText8232573838728338777" style="display:none">One would expect with a storyline revolving around an average Joe struggling to ransom his kidnapped wife back that it'd be super intense and keep me on the edge of my seat, right?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398005087ra/9356418.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It dragged on and on and the writing wasn't something I'd expect from a bestselling author. It was sketchy and the dialogue at times was just plain awkward.<br><br>There were some moments that made me sit up, but those were far and in-between and mostly had to do with the wife, Holly. The husband, Mitch was a fucking pansy and I hated him even after he grew balls at the very, <i>very</i> end of the book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398005087ra/9356419.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending was a happily-ever-after of the likes that have not been seen since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162543.Breaking_Dawn__Twilight___4_" title="Breaking Dawn (Twilight, #4) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Breaking Dawn</a>. I want <b>trauma</b>. I want <b>psychological pain</b>. Or at the very least, <b>signs of healing</b>. I don't want a chocolate syrup-coated sundae with fucking rainbow sprinkles. This is an Adult book, no? Then give me the bitter reality, don't airbrush it out. That's what I read romances for.<br><br>Needless to say, I will not be reading another Dean Koontz book anytime soon. Honestly, you'd be better off with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a>. Heck, even <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/19954.Christopher_Pike" title="Christopher Pike" rel="nofollow noopener">Christopher Pike</a> would be more entertaining than this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8232573838728338777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3801175501730753901">An excellent tale of suspense focusing on the strength of love, the power of madness and the impact evil can have on the innocent. An incredible opening and equally entertaining finish let down only by a slightly slower middle section. Te expected comeraderie between the book's title character and the local Detective failed to eventuate, which i found a trifle disappointing. But despite these criticisms, THE HUSBAND is one of the better books Mr Koontz has ever written. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5108990313914395591">This book was recommended to me by a co-worker after I let him borrow my Life Expectancy copy. Compared to that, this was a huge disappointment.<br/><br/>The first hundred or so pages dragged on, but I kept reading in hopes of it becoming something more entertaining.   <span id="freeText5108990313914395591" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by a co-worker after I let him borrow my Life Expectancy copy. Compared to that, this was a huge disappointment.<br /><br />The first hundred or so pages dragged on, but I kept reading in hopes of it becoming something more entertaining. I think it had the potential, but just fell short.<br /><br />After the twist of his brother's involvement, I thought for sure the plot would get thicker and more complicated. But instead the book just plodded on with the same mediocre sense of suspense.<br /><br />Though the part that still looms in my mind takes place at the end of Part I. Mitch gets stuffed into the trunk of the old Chrysler and the lid is slammed. The end of the next chapter describes Holly hearing a trunk lid close. I'm assuming this wasn't a coincidence. Was she being kept above the mobster's garage? Was Anson in on her kidnapping? This would have been more interesting. Alas it was never brought up again or explained.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11850471678610865853">"Be sure. Evil has a cockroach endurance. Be sure." --- so true.<br/><br/>This is my 9th Dean Koontz book but yet between this and the last it's been years. I'm not exactly sure why I strayed away from Koontz but I'm glad I rediscovered him. I listened to this book on audio and even though I wasn't entirely thrilled with the narrator, I got past it. The story was about a guy whose wife had been kidnapped and was ransomed for 2 million dollars. The guy was a gardener. Where would he get that kind of money?</span>
  <span id="freeText11850471678610865853" style="display:none">"Be sure. Evil has a cockroach endurance. Be sure." --- so true.<br /><br />This is my 9th Dean Koontz book but yet between this and the last it's been years. I'm not exactly sure why I strayed away from Koontz but I'm glad I rediscovered him. I listened to this book on audio and even though I wasn't entirely thrilled with the narrator, I got past it. The story was about a guy whose wife had been kidnapped and was ransomed for 2 million dollars. The guy was a gardener. Where would he get that kind of money? Hence, the story begins. Really good book. </span>

        <a title="The Face of Your Father" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Face of Your Father" href="/user/show/79119566-the-face-of-your-father">The Face of Your Father</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_228934707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228934707" />
    <a title="Christopher Jones" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6819702-christopher-jones"><img alt="Christopher Jones" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328304964p2/6819702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228934707?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Jones" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Jones" href="/user/show/6819702-christopher-jones">Christopher Jones</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007226566" href="/book/show/906896.The_Husband">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer228934707&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228934707" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6761102736837505254">My first novel by Koontz and it might've been my last had I not made it my life's mission to figure out why the guy was popular. <br/><br/>Characters: There are a generous handful of them. Mitch, the gardener protagonist. His brother. His parents. The Detective Taggart. The kidnappers. None of them are really developed, save for Mitch: his developmental arc centers around his realization that evil exists....except he already seemed to know it existed already. <br/><br/>For all Koontz rantings about the fact that ev</span>
  <span id="freeText6761102736837505254" style="display:none">My first novel by Koontz and it might've been my last had I not made it my life's mission to figure out why the guy was popular. <br /><br />Characters: There are a generous handful of them. Mitch, the gardener protagonist. His brother. His parents. The Detective Taggart. The kidnappers. None of them are really developed, save for Mitch: his developmental arc centers around his realization that evil exists....except he already seemed to know it existed already. <br /><br />For all Koontz rantings about the fact that evil exists (he honestly seems to think his readers don't know this already), he doesn't say what the nature of evil is. In Relentless, it seemed it was "progressive ideology" going against "tradition." But in The Husband, he doesn't really say at all. I think the most obvious sources would be selfishness (on the part of the perpetrator) and apathy (on the part of the witnesses), but what do I know? <br /><br />Plot: Centers around Mitch's wife being kidnapped. He has to find $2 million in cash in order to get her back alive. It sounds exciting. It isn't. Mitch doesn't have to pull off any heists or anything Hollywoodish like that. He just gets it from his brother. He gets kidnapped and nearly killed at one point and the "hunting" chapter following that had the potential to be interesting but wasn't. Mitch overthinks a lot of his decisions, over-examining every single detail and it slows the action to a crawl. Except there isn't really that much action to speak of. There's a couple shootings. A couple tazings. That's it.<br /><br />Climax: Boring. The main problem is that the kidnappers totally suck. <br /><br />The dogwalker at the beginning: he is one of the kidnappers. He's dumb enough to agree to walk a dog out across the street, thinking that his buddies will shoot the dog. Of course they shoot him instead, improving their share of the 2 million. <br /><br />One of the kidnappers stalks Mitch, but then is killed by falling boxes in a freak accident (real significant threat these people are). Then another kidnapper (the craziest one) grows paranoid and murders the rest of the men holding Holly hostage. <br /><br />So now, Mitch has to fight only one of them. That kind of thing lowers the tension instead of raising it. Sure, Holly is now trapped in a room with a guy that is giving off more rapey-vibes than the bad guy from Lovely Bones. But after the third or fourth conversation in which he doesn't so much as touch her, that threat is also reduced.<br /><br />The final, climactic battle should be the most difficult, most painful fight. Or at least, it should be both painful and difficult. Here, Mitch shoots the crazy guy off a motorcycle. The exchange lasted two pages. Compare this with Lighting's final battle. Nuff said.<br /><br />Prose: People other than those who are fans of James "I'm too lazy to write my own books" Patterson, will find the prose and format jarring. Short sentences. Like this. Short paragraphs too. Chapters three maybe four pages long. This is one of Koontz's recent entries that doesn't have long-wided descriptions about the environment simply because Koontz doesn't want the paragraph to be more than three or four lines long. The form was so bad I wasn't even aware of the political message at the time.<br /><br />Another thing that stood out to me when I first read it: squeaky clean language. People in real life swear. The average person in real life swears a lot. I have heard people swear while making statements under oath. I have heard lawyers swear in their own offices with the doors open. Criminals probably swear even more than that. <br /><br />The worst thing people say in The Husband is shit and bitch and even that is relatively occasional. The kidnappers (hardened veteran criminals) refer to Holly as "honey." Huh? People get betrayed by loved ones, criminals get fastened to chairs and trapped in laundry rooms and nobody says the word "fuck"?<br /><br />I get that you don't want it to be a crutch or make it be distracting. But when you are billed as a writer of "suspense" exploring the darkness of humanity, you can't be afraid of it like Tolkien is going to rise out of his grave and take your Catholic card away.<br /><br />With the lack of detailed violence and clean language, the end result is that The Husband reads more like young adult fiction. <br /><br />Conclusion: Not recommended. <br /><br />Update: I've actually reread it a little bit, after reading stuff like Lightning, and Frankenstein and Odd Thomas, and the Door to December. And I've read previews for stuff like Dragon Tears and Phantoms and By the Light of the Moon and Life Expectancy.<br /><br />It really is just such a plain-Jane novel from an author known to use sci-fi and government conspiracies and supernatural stuff. Literally anyone could've written such a basic kidnapping story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6761102736837505254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_233382490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233382490" />
    <a title="James Mourgos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3115573-james-mourgos"><img alt="James Mourgos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383847143p2/3115573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233382490?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Mourgos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Mourgos" href="/user/show/3115573-james-mourgos">James Mourgos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3115573-james-mourgos?shelf=books-i-hated">books-i-hated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233382490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14990128533412930699">First Impressions: <br/><br/>What I liked about The Husband has to do with the husband's reactions to the news that his wife has been kidnapped and the kidnappers seem to have unlimited resources and can kill him at any time. <br/><br/>Plots (some spoilers):<br/><br/>His name is Mitch, and he lives a good life as a gardener. He knows he does not have the money. Later the criminals get him to get his brother Anson involved, who, it turns out, is a criminal himself. The kidnappers know this and want to pull one over on Anson. </span>
  <span id="freeText14990128533412930699" style="display:none">First Impressions: <br /><br />What I liked about The Husband has to do with the husband's reactions to the news that his wife has been kidnapped and the kidnappers seem to have unlimited resources and can kill him at any time. <br /><br />Plots (some spoilers):<br /><br />His name is Mitch, and he lives a good life as a gardener. He knows he does not have the money. Later the criminals get him to get his brother Anson involved, who, it turns out, is a criminal himself. The kidnappers know this and want to pull one over on Anson. <br /><br />Despite these criminals thinking they have it all under control, Mitch finds deep inside himself the balls to do something about it, including killing (in self defense, of course) and stealing to get the money together. <br /><br />Dean Koontz does get into a sub-plot of Mitch and his brother and their relationship with their parents who had an unusual way of raising children, including a sense-deprivation room that was designed to "help" but really it was to break them. The book really does not explore this fascinating item very well. We meet his dad, Daniel, but his mother Kathy is barely mentioned and not at all developed. They were caricatures to me and not really well-developed, despite them being a critical influence on Mitch and Anson and their sisters (who are not even mentioned until near the end of the book and even then not developed). <br /><br />The book does get into the criminal minds and only fully develops the last guy – the one with a spiritual bent and who has no problem killing people so that they may attain "ascendancy". <br /><br />Holly is the kidnapped wife who we don't even meet until well into the book – at least not to any great degree. She too has depth and needs to reach in for strength and is surprised to find that she too can be devious. <br /><br />Why The Book Fails:<br /><br />The book fails for me in touching on certain characters (Julian Campbell with his child porn business is never developed, so you have no sympathy nor care that the guy gets his later) and leaves a huge plot hole at the end (Mitch kills and steals and then near the last chapter he has kids and is friends with the Columbo-like detective – huh? What happened?). Too much landscape vocabulary to show us how smart and real Koontz is, but does not add to the tale. <br /><br />Conclusion: Not Dean's best, though I do appreciate his writing a "straight" novel. However, I much prefer his supernatural stuff. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14990128533412930699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41082644" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41082644" />
    <a title="Graham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1760824-graham"><img alt="Graham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380743323p2/1760824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41082644?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graham" href="/user/show/1760824-graham">Graham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007226566" href="/book/show/906896.The_Husband">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1760824-graham?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41082644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12026156638650553439">Although Dean Koontz isn’t quite as successful as Stephen King, he’s certainly been writing for a long time now, almost as long as King himself. In the old days he used to do supernatural horrors but these days he seems to have re-branded himself as a thriller writer, and there’s no doubting that he’s extremely prolific – I see new books coming out from him all the time. The Husband was released a couple of years ago and it’s familiar territory for thriller fans: a seemingly innocuous man finds </span>
  <span id="freeText12026156638650553439" style="display:none">Although Dean Koontz isn’t quite as successful as Stephen King, he’s certainly been writing for a long time now, almost as long as King himself. In the old days he used to do supernatural horrors but these days he seems to have re-branded himself as a thriller writer, and there’s no doubting that he’s extremely prolific – I see new books coming out from him all the time. The Husband was released a couple of years ago and it’s familiar territory for thriller fans: a seemingly innocuous man finds himself caught up in a whole heap of trouble when his wife is kidnapped and held for ransom.<br /><br />What follows is a novel that’s chock-full of twists and turns and an easy writing style that makes it an effortless read. The problem is that it all seems so familiar. I love thrillers but this type of ‘ransom’ plot really has been done to death, and the little tweaks and touches that Koontz adds to the plot don’t really do anything new. I know there are no new stories left in the world but I think a little more imagination would have gone a long way.<br /><br />Still, there are positives. The everyman hero is appealing and the characters well drawn. Koontz ably hides the motivation of supporting characters and you’re never quite sure who’s good or who’s bad. The opening chapters of the novel are extremely suspenseful and packed with shocking surprises, and up to the mid-way point it’s a bit of a rollercoaster read. Unfortunately, the book starts falling apart at around this mark as the author runs out of steam and resorts to hefty padding to up the page length. There’s a whole monologue on fossil collecting to endure and lots of other unnecessary elements that don’t really add much to the way of the story. The ending is also a little tired, as the bad guy and the good guy duel it out to the death and one of those “recurring villain” deaths so beloved of Hollywood horror movies where the bad guy keeps coming back to life. It’s clichéd and a little dull, and it feels it.<br /><br />So a great first half and a subdued second half equal a distinctly average novel. It’s okay but far from the pulse-pounding read I was hoping for. Koontz, you can do better than this, and turning autopilot off would be a great start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12026156638650553439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1755703756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13042617957708179214">All my reviews are at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.jessicasreadingroom.com'>www.jessicasreadingroom.com</a><br/><br/>The premise of the book catches your attention and pulls you in. The actual novel not so much. <br/><br/>The Husband is divided into three parts. The first part is very good. Mitchell (Mitch) Rafferty is a landscaper and working a job when he receives a call that his wife has been kidnapped. And the kidnappers want $2 Million cash. He has 60 hours to get the money and they know he is a gardener with limited means. They let him know they are serious by shoo</span>
  <span id="freeText13042617957708179214" style="display:none">All my reviews are at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jessicasreadingroom.com">www.jessicasreadingroom.com</a><br /><br />The premise of the book catches your attention and pulls you in. The actual novel not so much. <br /><br />The Husband is divided into three parts. The first part is very good. Mitchell (Mitch) Rafferty is a landscaper and working a job when he receives a call that his wife has been kidnapped. And the kidnappers want $2 Million cash. He has 60 hours to get the money and they know he is a gardener with limited means. They let him know they are serious by shooting a man walking a dog. And like other novels similar to this, no cops or they kill his wife.<br /><br />Here starts Mitch’s journey to rush to get the money. Will he make it to the deadline? Will he get the money? Will he save his wife? What will happen?<br /><br />The book’s direction falls flat. There is a twist that you find out early on who is responsible for this happening. <br /><br />There are several subplots, one involves his family and his childhood. This includes a sense-deprivation room that his parents used on Mitch and his siblings growing up. You do get to see how experiencing that affects them in both extremes, good and bad. This could be a fabulous plot to be used… in another book.<br /><br />Overall, I could not recommend this book. I did keep listening to it to see what would happen. When I finished it I did not really have an opinion of the book. This was disappointing as I was hoping it would keep me on the edge of my seat and have me wanting more. <br /><br />This is my second Koontz book, the first was Life Expectancy which I had rated four stars. Despite being disappointed in The Husband, I will read Koontz again. <br /><br />***I rated this books at 2.5 stars, but Goodreads doesn't let you do 1/2 star ratings.</span>

<div id="review_1730530104" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1730530104" />
    <a title="Carl Alves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1435359-carl-alves"><img alt="Carl Alves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442608000p2/1435359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1730530104?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carl Alves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carl Alves" href="/user/show/1435359-carl-alves">Carl Alves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1730530104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12448019533751647809">I decided to read this novel with some reluctance since of late I seem to be disappointed with Dean Koontz’s novels. I read them because occasionally (at least with his older works) he hits a home run and the novel is terrific. The premise of the book is interesting enough. Mitch Rafferty’s wife is kidnapped and the kidnappers demand two millions dollars, something that is difficult since he is only a simple gardener.<br/><br/>The problem is the characterization in the novel. The novel is filled with one </span>
  <span id="freeText12448019533751647809" style="display:none">I decided to read this novel with some reluctance since of late I seem to be disappointed with Dean Koontz’s novels. I read them because occasionally (at least with his older works) he hits a home run and the novel is terrific. The premise of the book is interesting enough. Mitch Rafferty’s wife is kidnapped and the kidnappers demand two millions dollars, something that is difficult since he is only a simple gardener.<br /><br />The problem is the characterization in the novel. The novel is filled with one weak character after another. The first is Mitch. He is a nice enough guy, but he falls into the category of someone who isn’t capable. What I mean is that in a difficult situation with violence and lives on the line, he is not the type of character that would be able to come through. He is a bit of a wimp. The bad guy characters are even worse. Realism and dreadfully poor villain characters have always been Koontz’s downfall, and that’s the case here as well. An example is Mitch’s brother. It is impossible to believe that he’s this hardcore gangster without Mitch ever having a hint of that being the case. Also, his rationale of betraying his brother is just downright stupid. The even more villainous character is one of the kidnappers, and this character is just God awful. In the end, this novel did not deliver and I would recommend skipping it.<br /><br />Carl Alves - author of Conjesero</span>
  <a data-text-id="12448019533751647809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1260727509199484156">3 STARS<br/><br/>"What would you do for love? Would you die? Would you kill?<br/><br/>We have your wife. You can get her back for two million cash. Landscaper Mitchell Rafferty thinks it must be some kind of joke. He was in the middle of planting impatiens in the yard of one of his clients when his cell phone rang.   <span id="freeText1260727509199484156" style="display:none">3 STARS<br /><br />"What would you do for love? Would you die? Would you kill?<br /><br />We have your wife. You can get her back for two million cash. Landscaper Mitchell Rafferty thinks it must be some kind of joke. He was in the middle of planting impatiens in the yard of one of his clients when his cell phone rang. Now he's standing in a normal suburban neighborhood on a bright summer day, having a phone conversation out of his darkest nightmare.<br /><br />Whoever is on the other end of the line is dead serious. He has Mitch's wife and he's named the price for her safe return. The caller doesn't care that Mitch runs a small two-man landscaping operation and has no way of raising such a vast sum. He's confident that Mitch will find a way.<br />If he loves his wife enough. . . Mitch does love her enough. He loves her more than life itself. He's got seventy-two hours to prove it. He has to find the two million by then. But he'll pay a lot more. He'll pay anything." (From Amazon) <br /><br />Koontz is getting less like Stephen King and more like Harlan Coben (more suspense than thriller). He writes well in both sort of genres.</span>

<div id="review_1803640379" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1803640379" />
    <a title=" Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Jenn Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Schu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18916088-jenn-schu"><img alt=" Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Jenn Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Schu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560021036p2/18916088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1803640379?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Jenn Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Schu" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Jenn Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Schu" href="/user/show/18916088-jenn-schu"> Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Jenn Ƹ̴Ӂ̴Ʒ Schu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18916088-jenn-schu?shelf=fallintoreading2016">fallintoreading2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18916088-jenn-schu?shelf=snakesandladders">snakesandladders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18916088-jenn-schu?shelf=fallreading2016">fallreading2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18916088-jenn-schu?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1803640379" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1791466743407093595">Suspense filled Koontz story about what a man will do to save his beloved wife from kidnappers. The book has the typical dysfunctional characters from thugs to sociopaths as well as a bit of violence. The story is a page turner, but I also found myself speed reading over several parts of the book. The skimmed areas weren't poorly written, I just found a few segments to be uninteresting. And, like many Koontz stories, a happy-ish ending.<br/>2.75 stars<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2298047466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2298047466" />
    <a title="Claire Maloy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59397897-claire-maloy"><img alt="Claire Maloy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2298047466?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire Maloy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire Maloy" href="/user/show/59397897-claire-maloy">Claire Maloy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2298047466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1071491097761857705">“The Husband,” by Dean Koontz, is a very sketchy novel. A man finds out this kidnapper takes his wife. He needs to give the guy 2 million dollars, cash “or else.” He tries everything he can to find money, but he’s only a gardener. Where will he get that kind of money? I didn’t really like this book. Most of the action was in the beginning so the rest was not as interesting as that. Since all the entertainment was first, there was none left for the rest, except the end. Also this book was bloody </span>
  <span id="freeText1071491097761857705" style="display:none">“The Husband,” by Dean Koontz, is a very sketchy novel. A man finds out this kidnapper takes his wife. He needs to give the guy 2 million dollars, cash “or else.” He tries everything he can to find money, but he’s only a gardener. Where will he get that kind of money? I didn’t really like this book. Most of the action was in the beginning so the rest was not as interesting as that. Since all the entertainment was first, there was none left for the rest, except the end. Also this book was bloody and intense. It was even frightening at parts. I like mystery books, but this one may have been too much. I like the kind of mystery where the killer/kidnapper is hidden in the story. Like they seem innocent, but aren’t. This one, you didn’t know the name, but you knew who it was. They weren’t trying to act innocent. Plus, they never told you his name. I did like the adventure. When he did everything he could to get money. Also, it was never made you bored. Even though the middle is slower than the beginning, it was still action packed. I think the theme for this is love is stronger than hate. He loved his wife and did everything to help her. The kidnappers did it for money, no love there, just hate. Love always wins in the end. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1071491097761857705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N7x+dcM30Nz0Geo5P4mRDUGG/xPmMPL0jXTqVJGjfw3DeQvHl8WXN6gJbJcykKnCjHBj4t0wJG6oPlqf1Ce60Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('awXPF7nQVS1LAfM0bjgJnRIPJJXZYCBCq/DrdoLXw9KfwLql7SISxhcRdZpjITFS3/m4ZOJg9tiOulu9x1MGDg==')})
  }
//]]>

But how did young Winston become Churchill? What gave him the strength to take on the superior force of Nazi Germany when bombs rained on London and so many others had caved? In The Storm of War, Andrew Roberts gave us a tantalizing glimpse of Churchill the war leader. Now, at last, we have the full and definitive biography, as personally revealing as it is compulsively readable, about one of the great leaders of all time.\n\nRoberts was granted exclusive access to extensive new material: the transcripts of war cabinet meetings - the equivalent of the Nixon and JFK tapes - diaries, letters, unpublished memoirs, and detailed notes taken by the king after their bi-weekly meetings. Having read every one of Churchill\'s letters, including deeply personal ones that Churchill\'s son Randolph had previously chosen to withhold, and spoken to more than one hundred people who knew or worked with him, Roberts identifies the hidden forces fueling Churchill\'s drive. Churchill put his faith in the British Empire and fought as hard to preserve it as he did to defend London. Having started his career in India and South Africa, he understood better than most idealists how hard it can be to pacify reluctant people far from home.\n\nWe think of Churchill as a hero of the age of mechanized warfare, but Roberts\'s masterwork reveals that he has as much to teach us about the challenges we face today and the fundamental values of courage, tenacity, leadership, and moral With the Denton wives remaining tight-lipped, Josie’s only hope is a secret meet-up with a terrified woman willing to talk. But she is murdered moments before giving Josie crucial information. It’s clear that someone is prepared to keep on killing to stop the truth from getting out.\n\nDigging deep into memories of her own past with Ray is the only advantage Josie has on this twisted   <span id="freeText6030382733920564129" style="display:none">Acknowledged as "America's most popular suspense novelist" (Rolling Stone) and as one of today's most celebrated and successful writers, Dean Ray Koontz has earned the devotion of millions of readers around the world and the praise of critics everywhere for tales of character, mystery, and adventure that strike to the core of what it means to be human.<br /><br />Dean, the author of many #1 New York Times bestsellers, lives in Southern California with his wife, Gerda, their golden retriever, Elsa, and the enduring spirit of their goldens, Trixie and Anna.<br /> <br />Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial">Facebook.com/DeanKoontzOfficial</a><br />Twitter: @DeanKoontz<br />Website: DeanKoontz.com </span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
